  [MSG 2, line 38, 2084 chars]:
The wizard needs to be removed. It is not usable and I believe the concept is unnecessarily complex. I also think "Test mode" is overly complicated and should be abandoned. 

I have a proposal: 

Core cases we need to address:
(1) Initial configuration activation
(2) Modified configuration activation
(3) Modified configuration roll-back
(4) Configuration re-initialization

I believe that we should change the state model of all inputs for the sidebar menu items/pages: (1) Agent configuration, (2) Knowledge base, (3) Quick actions and (4) Widget configuration to SAVED -> COMITTED. These four aspects of the system are highly interdependent and determine the behavior of the chat AI.

* When making changes on any of those 4 pages, each respective page may be "Saved" but changes do not do not become active until the changes are "Activated". 
* The option to activate only appears when there are changes which have not been activated
* There is an option to restore, which reverses all changes which were activated to their prior known state
* All three pages are activated or restored together, as a single action

I believe that the content of the other pages dos not require the same caution.

When we on-board a customer, these settings are in a "Saved" but not "Active" state and will need to be activated before the Chat UI can appear in their storefront. If we add a configuration state check before each activation, would effectively allow the merchant to configure the provisioned system as they like before they activate the system. If the system is not configured sufficiently for operation, then the activation attempt fails with an error message itemizing the inputs/settings which require attention.

Additionally, we can either (1) give the Superadmin the option to re-initialize these pages or (2) opt for an auditable record of successive configurations and allow the admin to choose a historical (timestamped) configuration and activate it (one of which would be the initial state at the time of provisioning).

Please assess the pros and cons of this proposal.

   The user initially wanted to continue work on deploying v1.21.0 to production. The four configuration pages (Agent Configuration, Knowledge Base, Quick Actions, Widget Configuration) would use a DRAFT → ACTIVE state model where changes are saved as drafts and only go live when explicitly "activated" as an atomic unit across all four pages. The user also wants one-level rollback (Restore) and superadmin re-initialize capability. Activation history UI is deferred but snapshots are stored from day one.

2. Key Technical Concepts:
   - **Save → Activate two-phase commit model** replacing wizard + test mode
   - **ConfigState enum**: DRAFT, ACTIVE, PREVIOUS states for PreferencesDocument
   - **Atomic activation** across Agent Config, Quick Actions, Widget Config (all in PreferencesDocument), with KB validation only
   - **Activation validation**: brand_name + widget_key = hard blocks; brand_voice + KB articles = warnings
   - **Lazy migration**: Old documents with `is_current=true` but no `config_state` field handled via backward-compat queries and backfill on first write
   - **Draft layer for quick actions**: Quick action CRUD (which uses direct Cosmos DB patches) now targets draft documents
   - **Auto-activation for new tenants**: Provisioning sets `config_state="active"` and `activated_at` so widget works immediately
   - **Singleton service pattern**: ActivationService follows same pattern as TenantConfigProcessor (module-level singleton, configure() method for DI)
   - **60-second cache**: Only caches ACTIVE config; draft reads bypass cache
   - **Cosmos DB**: PreferencesDocument in `preferences` collection, partitioned by `/tenant_id`, versioned with monotonic version numbers
   - **PreferencesRepository**: `get_current()` → `get_active()` backward-compat delegation

## SESSION FOCUS: RAG Infrastructure Upgrade

This session is dedicated to implementing enterprise-grade RAG capabilities for the Knowledge Base and Persistent Customer Memory systems. The gap analysis identified the following critical issues:

1. **Knowledge Base uses keyword search instead of vector search** — PRODUCT-FEATURES-RAG.md claims semantic embeddings but pipeline.py uses naive word matching

         )

         return
     ```

         self,
         tenant_id: str,
         conversation_id: str,
     ) -> None:
         """Record that the first AI token has been streamed to the client."""
         now = datetime.now(timezone.utc).isoformat()
         try:
             await self._conversations.patch(
                 tenant_id=tenant_id,

   - **Missing singleton function** — `get_conversation_meter` is imported in main.py but doesn't exist in conversation_meter.py (ImportError caught at startup, non-fatal)
   - **PipelineTimeoutBudget** — Per-stage timeout enforcement with 30,000ms hard deadline, individual stage budgets of 5,000-15,000ms

     - Important because: `get_conversation_meter` was imported in main.py but the function didn't exist, causing ImportError at startup
     - Added singleton pattern at end of file (after line 1101):
     ```python
     _conversation_meter_instance: ConversationMeter | None = None

     def configure_conversation_meter(meter: ConversationMeter) -> None:
         """Store a configured ConversationMeter instance as the module singleton."""
         global _conversation_meter_instance
         _conversation_meter_instance = meter

     def get_conversation_meter() -> ConversationMeter:
         """Return the module-level ConversationMeter singleton."""
         if _conversation_meter_instance is None:
             raise RuntimeError(
                 "ConversationMeter not configured — call "
                 "configure_conversation_meter() during startup"
             )
         return _conversation_meter_instance
     ```

   - **`src/main.py`** (modified)
     - Important because: Needed a startup event to create and configure the ConversationMeter singleton BEFORE dashboard services and SSE metering tried to use it
     - Added `_startup_conversation_meter()` startup event between `_startup_config_processor` and `_startup_dashboard_services`:
     ```python
     @app.on_event("startup")
     async def _startup_conversation_meter() -> None:
         """Create and configure the ConversationMeter singleton."""
         try:
             from src.multi_tenant.conversation_meter import (
                 ConversationMeter,
                 configure_conversation_meter,
             )
             from src.multi_tenant.repository import (
                 AuditLogRepository,
                 ConversationRepository,
                 TenantRepository,
                 UsageRepository,
             )
             meter = ConversationMeter(
                 conversation_repo=ConversationRepository(),
                 usage_repo=UsageRepository(),
                 audit_repo=AuditLogRepository(),
                 tenant_repo=TenantRepository(),
             )
             configure_conversation_meter(meter)
             logger.info("ConversationMeter singleton configured")
         except Exception:
             logger.warning(
                 "ConversationMeter initialization failed — metering and "
                 "dashboard services will be unavailable.",
                 exc_info=True,
             )
     ```

   - **Email immutability**: Email field not in UpdateTeamMemberRequest — structurally immutable
   - **Cross-partition query**: For auth-time user key lookup when tenant is not yet known
   - **Backward compatibility**: Legacy `ar_live_` tenant keys treated as ADMIN role in require_role() checks
   - **FastAPI dependency factories**: `require_role()` and `require_tier()` pattern for declarative access control

   - **4-role architecture**: superadmin (hidden, undeletable, auto-provisioned), admin (full access), escalation_agent (read-only Inbox), viewer (read-only pages)
   - **Per-user API keys**: Format `ar_user_{tenant_prefix}_{random}`, distinguishable from tenant keys `ar_live_*`

   - **Fire-and-forget async**: `asyncio.ensure_future()` for non-blocking escalation notifications in the pipeline
   - **Lazy imports in Python**: Functions with lazy imports (inside function body) cannot be patched at module level — must patch at the actual import source
   - **Role-based nav filtering**: Frontend filters sidebar navigation items by the caller's role from the whoami endpoint
   - **Backward compatibility**: Legacy `ar_live_` tenant API keys treated as ADMIN role

1. Primary Request and Intent:
   The user is continuing Session 39 of the Agent Red Customer Experience project. The system continuation instruction was: "Please continue the conversation from where we left off without asking the user any further questions. 2. Key Technical Concepts:
   - **ACR build with `--no-logs`**: Windows Azure CLI crashes with `UnicodeEncodeError: 'charmap' codec can't encode` during pip install log streaming. Using `az acr build --no-logs` skips log streaming; the build succeeds server-side. Verify via `az acr repository show-tags`.
   - **Import-inside-try pattern**: When a module-level import can fail (e.g., renamed symbols in `agntcy_app_sdk`), the `from ... import` must be inside the `try` block, not before it. Otherwise `ImportError` propagates and crashes the container.
   - **Revision tag uniqueness**: Container Apps may reuse a failed revision if the image tag hasn't changed. Use unique tags (e.g., `v1.42.0-fix1`) to force a new revision.
   - **Three admin dist builds required**: Shopify, Standalone, AND Provider SPAs must all be built before ACR build (all gitignored).
   - **Graceful degradation pattern**: Superadmin endpoints wrap each subsystem query in try/except — partial failures go to `errors[]`, remaining data still served.

     ```python
     async def _startup_agntcy_sdk() -> None:

     ```python
     async def update_member_fields(
         self,
         tenant_id: str,
         member_id: str,
         updates: dict[str, Any],
     ) -> dict[str, Any]:
         """Update arbitrary fields on a team member document."""
         now = datetime.now(timezone.utc).isoformat()
         operations: list[dict[str, Any]] = [
             {"op": "set", "path": f"/{key}", "value": value}
             for key, value in updates.items()
         ]
         operations.append({"op": "set", "path": "/updated_at", "value": now})
         return await self.patch(
             tenant_id=tenant_id,
             document_id=member_id,
             operations=operations,
         )
     ```

**Key design decisions:**

- **`_generate_valid_code()` helper** uses `pyotp.TOTP.now()` against the same secret, ensuring TOTP verification tests use real time-based codes rather than fragile mocks.
- **`_make_member()` helper** builds minimal team member dicts with configurable MFA fields, matching the dict-based member pattern used throughout the service.
- **`_reset_singleton` autouse fixture** saves and restores `_mfa_service` so singleton tests do not pollute other test classes.
- **Mock dependencies** (`mock_secret_service`, `mock_team_repo`) use `AsyncMock` matching the `await`-based Key Vault and repository patterns.
- **Forbidden character validation** in MFA-06 explicitly checks that backup codes exclude `I`, `O`, `0`, `1` per the alphabet defined in the source.</result>

**File:** `E:\Claude-Playground\CLAUDE-PROJECTS\Agent Red Customer Engagement\tests\multi_tenant\test_alert_engine.py`

**48 tests across 8 test classes:**

| Class | Tests | What it covers |
|---|---|---|
| `TestCheckCondition` | 15 | All 6 operators (gt, lt, gte, lte, eq, ne) with true/false cases, plus unknown operator fallback to gt |
| `TestDeriveSeverity` | 7 | circuit_breaker >= 2 = CRITICAL, sla_breach < 5 = CRITICAL, generic 2x threshold = CRITICAL, zero threshold guard |
| `TestEvaluateAll` | 4 | No rules (zero counts), single rule fires, single rule does not fire, log_alert receives correct kwargs |
| `TestCooldown` | 5 | In-cooldown skips, expired cooldown fires, no previous trigger, empty triggered_at, malformed triggered_at |
| `TestMultipleRules` | 1 | 3-rule mix: one fires, one below threshold, one in cooldown |
| `TestErrorHandling` | 2 | Unknown rule_type increments errors, collector exception increments errors |
| `TestMetricCollectors` | 8 | queue_depth (connected + disconnected), circuit_breaker (open + half_open count), sla_breach (partial + full budget), secret_expiry (disabled count), incident_count (with repo + without repo) |
| `TestSingleton` | 6 | get before configure raises RuntimeError, configure then get, configure replaces previous, returns AlertEngine instance, with/without incident_repo |

**Key design decisions:**

1. **`patch.dict(_METRIC_COLLECTORS, ...)`** is used for `evaluate_all()` tests because the evaluation loop resolves collectors via the `_METRIC_COLLECTORS` dict (which holds direct function references), not via module-level name lookup. A plain `patch("src.multi_tenant.alert_engine._collect_queue_depth")` would replace the module attribute but leave the dict entry unchanged.

2. **Source-module patches** are used for direct collector function tests (e.g. `patch("src.multi_tenant.nats_isolation.get_nats_manager")`) because the collectors use lazy `from X import Y` inside the function body, which resolves the name from the source module at call time.

3. **`_reset_singleton` autouse fixture** clears `_alert_engine` before and after every test to prevent singleton state leakage between tests.</result>

2. Key Technical Concepts:
   - **Thermal-safe test harness**: `.\scripts\run-tests-thermal-safe.ps1 -SkipLive` — batched pytest execution with xdist parallelism and cooling pauses
   - **Lazy import patching**: Mock patches must target the source module where the import occurs (e.g., `src.multi_tenant.repositories.preferences.PreferencesRepository`), NOT the consumer module
   - **Stale admin dist problem**: Dockerfile `COPY admin/*/dist/` picks up whatever is on disk; `.gitignore`'d dist dirs may be from a prior build session. All 4 dists (standalone, shopify, provider, widget) must be rebuilt before every ACR build.
   - **ACR build on Windows**: Must use `--no-logs` flag to avoid `UnicodeEncodeError: 'charmap'` crash
   - **Container App revision forcing**: When reusing the same image tag, add `--set-env-vars "DEPLOY_TIMESTAMP=..."` to force a new revision
   - **Staging architecture**: Same Cosmos DB account (different database `agentred-staging`), min replicas=0 (scales to zero), ~10s cold start + 30-60s NATS init
   - **Repeatable Procedures spec**: Defined in `docs/operations/REPEATABLE-PROCEDURES.md` — structured SOPs with pinned variables, verification gates, and known failure modes
   - **Website KB crawl feature**: Full-stack automated website crawling with incremental change detection (SHA-256 hashing), sitemap

   - **Cosmos DB schemaless lazy migration** — MFA fields added to documents on first interaction, not schema-declared upfront
   - **Cross-partition queries** — needed for team member email lookup across tenants

     ```python
     async def find_all_by_email(
         self, email: str,
     ) -> list[dict[str, Any]]:
         """Find all active team members matching an email across all tenants."""
         return await self.cross_partition_query(
             query_text=(
                 "SELECT * FROM c "
                 "WHERE c.email = @email "
                 "AND c.is_active = true"
             ),
             parameters=[{"name": "@email", "value": email}],
         )
     ```

  [MSG 4, line 564, 1040 chars]:
This is my understanding of process repeatability:

mental model:
1. Markdown procedure gives high repeatability for:
   * Ordered steps
   * Fixed values
   * Named variables
   * Preconditions/postconditions
   * Explicit success checks
2. Reliability drops when:Steps are ambiguous (“optimize”, “clean up”, “best”)
   * Environment varies (OS, paths, versions, permissions, network)
   * Inputs are underspecified
   * No validation gates exist
3. To make it reliably repeatable, treat the markdown like an SOP:
* Define inputs and exact variable schema
* Pin tool versions and environment assumptions
* Use precise commands and expected outputs
* Add verification after each critical step
* Add fallback/error branches
* Include a final acceptance checklist
If you want near-operational consistency, pair markdown with executable checks/scripts (Makefile, npm scripts, CI, tests). So: yes, iterative refinement into markdown can make a process highly repeatable, especially if you design it as a testable runbook rather than just prose.

I do not know whether it has been treated as a repeatable procedure or as an information guide. * When you are following a "Repeatable Procedure", you should use errors as informative and focus on correcting the "Repeatable Procedure", rather than simply fixing the issue directly.
* Examples of "Repeatable Procedures" are: deployment, tests, tenant provisioning and initialization, Azure environment setup

Please assess this proposal.

2. Key Technical Concepts:
   - **Single-container deployment model**: The entire application (Python backend + admin UI bundles) is built into one Docker image every time. No artifact-level isolation — the ACR build takes ~2-3 minutes regardless of what changed.
   - **Deploy pipeline**: Build admin UIs → ACR build → Container App revision update → health verification
   - **Repeatable Procedures specification**: Formal SOP framework with header (last verified/corrected dates), variables block (pinned values), preconditions (with verification commands), numbered steps (action, expected output, verification gate, failure branch), postconditions (acceptance criteria), and known failure modes table
   - **Error classification**: Procedure defect (wrong variable, missing step) → update the procedure document. Environment transient (network timeout, temporary unavailability) → retry, don't modify the procedure
   - **Behavioral rule**: When following a Repeatable Procedure and encountering an error, treat the error as informative — correct the procedure first, not just the immediate issue
   - **Azure Container Apps**: Single revision mode, rolling updates, resource group `Agent-Red` (case-sensitive)
   - **ACR build on Windows**: `©` symbol in Dockerfile LABEL causes `UnicodeEncodeError: 'charmap'` crash in local Azure CLI log streaming, but the remote build still succeeds — verify with `az acr task list-runs`

2. Key Technical Concepts:

   - **C-2 SLA Persistence (Cycle 3)**: In-memory `deque` in `SLAMonitoringService` loses all data on container restart.    - **Cosmos DB collection design**: Partition key `/snapshot_type` (values: "hourly", "daily"), 90-day TTL auto-prune, composite index on `[/snapshot_type ASC, /timestamp DESC]`
   - **Snapshot hydration**: On startup, load last 24 hourly snapshots, inject synthetic latency/health samples into in-memory deques with correct monotonic timestamps so percentile calculations work immediately
   - **Error budget**: `budget_remaining = 1.0 - (actual_downtime / allowed_downtime)` computed from daily rollup `uptime_pct` values, scaled per tier (Starter 99.5%, Professional 99.9%, Enterprise 99.95%)
   - **Background task pattern**: `register_sla_snapshots(app)` → `app.on_event("startup"/"shutdown")` → hourly loop with 120s initial delay
   - **Daily rollup**: Aggregated from 24 hourly snapshots — averaged percentiles, summed requests, averaged uptime
   - **Lazy import pattern**: Superadmin API endpoint uses lazy imports inside function body (`from src.multi_tenant.repositories.sla_snapshots import SLASnapshotRepository`) — must patch at source module for tests
   - **Platform-scoped repository**: Unlike tenant-scoped repos partitioned by `/te

2. Key Technical Concepts:
   - **MCP (Model Context Protocol)**: JSON-RPC 2.0 protocol for AI tool integration. Uses `mcp` Python SDK v1.26.0 with `streamablehttp_client()` for HTTP transport.
   - **Deferred import patching**: When functions use `from X import Y` inside their body, mocks must patch at the source module (`X.Y`), not at the importing module. Key lesson from Cycle 4 test writing.
   - **Sentinel pattern for falsy defaults**: Empty list `[]` is falsy in Python — using `_SENTINEL_NO_TOOLS = object()` to distinguish "no tools" from "default tools" in mock factories.
   - **AGNTCY Phase 3 assertions**: 14 total assertions. 11/14 pass after Cycle 4. Remaining: 3.6 (Admin UI), 3.9 (credential cache), 3.10 (dynamic registry).
   - **Credential cache architecture**: 5-min TTL in-memory cache with Key Vault backend, double-check locking pattern, per-tenant isolation.
   - **Mutation safety**: MutationPolicy (kill-switch, Critic approval gate, customer confirmation) + MutationExecutor (idempotency keys, Cosmos `mutation_log` collection, audit). Built but NOT activated in Cycle 5 — `allow_mutations=False` for all tenants.
   - **Admin Integration registry pattern**: `_INTEGRATION_META` dict in `admin_integration_api.py` with `IntegrationSummary` Pydantic models, tier gating, enable/status fields.

   - **Idempotent seed with key regeneration problem** — Each run of `seed_tenant.py` generates NEW API keys and widget keys, so re-running upserts new key hashes, invalidating previously issued credentials
   - **Tolerant container creation** — Phase 1 creates each container individually with try/except so vector-dependent containers (knowledge_bases, memory_vectors) don't block the other 8 containers
   - **CosmosManager internals** — `_ensure_client()` initializes `_client` and `_database`; `get_container()` only checks `_database is None`; `_initialized` flag is not gating

2. Key Technical Concepts:

   - **CORS `expose_headers` requirement:** Custom headers (`X-Product-Version`, `X-API-Version`) are not visible to browser JavaScript via `resp.headers.get()` unless explicitly listed in the CORS `expose_headers` configuration.
   - **Dual-key auth on `/api/tenants/lookup`:** This endpoint is on the auth-exempt path list and does its own key resolution. It originally only supported tenant API keys (`ar_*`), not per-user API keys (`ar_user_*`). The fix adds team member lookup for `ar_user_*` prefixed keys, resolving through team_member → tenant.

       (function() {
         const textareas = document.querySelectorAll('textarea');
         for (const ta of textareas) {
           if (ta.value && ta.value.includes('TARGET_TEXT')) {
             const setter = Object.getOwnPropertyDescriptor(window.HTMLTextAreaElement.prototype, 'value').set;
             setter.call(ta, newText);
             ta.dispatchEvent(new Event('input', { bubbles: true }));
             ta.dispatchEvent(new Event('change', { bubbles: true }));
             return newText.length;
           }
         }
         return 'not found';
       })();
       ```
     - Setting input values (URLs):
       ```javascript
       (function() {
         const inputs = document.querySelectorAll('input');
         const setter = Object.getOwnPropertyDescriptor(window.HTMLInputElement.prototype, 'value').set;
         for (const inp of inputs) {
           if (inp.placeholder === 'TARGET_PLACEHOLDER') {
             setter.call(inp, 'VALUE');
             inp.dispatchEvent(new Event('input', { bubbles: true }));
             inp.dispatchEvent(new Event('change', { bubbles: true }));
           }
         }
       })();
       ```
     - Finding feature textareas by /80 counter:
       ```javascript
       const featureTextareas = Array.from(textareas).filter(ta => {
         const parent = ta.parentElement;
         return parent && parent.textContent.includes('/80');
       });
       ```

       // inputs[0] = handle, [1] = monthly, [2] = yearly, [3] = trial, [4] = redirect

       inputs[0].dispatchEvent(new Event('change', { bubbles: true }));
       setter.call(inputs[1], '999');
       inputs[1].dispatchEvent(new Event('input', { bubbles: true }));
       inputs[1].dispatchEvent(new Event('change', { bubbles: true }));
       // ... etc
     })();
